### Combined Build Configuration

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Combines multiple build configuration options, including environment variables, a custom command, and an output directory, along with other deployment settings like entrypoint and domains.

```json
{
  "config": {
    "entrypoint": "index.js",
    "domains": ["yourdomain.com"],
    "envVars": {
      "API_KEY": "your-api-key",
      "SOME_OTHER_KEY": "some-other-value"
    },
    "build": {
      "envVars": {
        "ANOTHER_VAR": "another-value"
      },
      "command": "npm run build",
      "outDir": "dist"
    }
  }
}
```

```json
    "start": "next start",
    "lint": "next lint"
  },
  "dependencies": {
    "next": "14.1.0",
    "react": "^18",
    "react-dom": "^18"
  },
  "devDependencies": {
    "@types/node": "^20",
    "@types/react": "^18",
    "@types/react-dom": "^18",
    "eslint": "^8",
    "eslint-config-next": "14.1.0",
    "typescript": "^5"
  }
}
```

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/schema",
  "type": "object",
  "properties": {
    "schemaVersion": {
      "type": "string",
      "enum": ["1.0"]
    },
    "outDir": {
      "type": "string"
    },
    "driver": {
      "type": "string",
      "enum": ["pg"]
    },
    "dbCredentials": {
      "type": "object",
      "properties": {
        "connectionString": {
          "type": "string"
        }
      },
      "required": ["connectionString"]
    }
  },
  "required": ["schemaVersion", "outDir", "driver", "dbCredentials"]
}
```

### Deploy Static Assets with Freestyle CLI

```bash
npx freestyle deploy --web main.ts --domain anydomain.style.dev
```

--------------------------------

### Deploy NextJS Project with Build

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Deploys a NextJS project to Freestyle with automatic framework detection and building enabled. Requires the 'freestyle-sandboxes' package and NextJS to be in standalone mode.

```ts
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";
import { prepareDirForDeploymentSync } from "freestyle-sandboxes/utils";

// Create a sandboxes client
const sandboxes = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!,
});

async function deploy() {
  await sandboxes.deployWeb(prepareDirForDeploymentSync("."), {
    // put whatever domains you want here
    domains: ["example.style.dev"],
    build: true, // This automatically detects the framework and configures/builds for you
  });
}

deploy();
```

--------------------------------

### Deploy Next.js Standalone Build with Freestyle Sandboxes SDK

Source: https://context7_llms

Deploys a Next.js project's standalone build using the Freestyle Sandboxes SDK, specifying the entrypoint and domains.

```javascript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";
import { prepareDirForDeploymentSync } from "freestyle-sandboxes/utils";

// Create a sandboxes client
const sandboxes = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!,
});

async function deploy() {
  await sandboxes.deployWeb(prepareDirForDeploymentSync(".next/standalone"), {
    entrypoint: "server.js",
    // put whatever domains you want here
    domains: ["example.style.dev"],
  });
}

deploy();
```

### Deploying Website from Files

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

```json
{
  "source" : {
    "kind": "files",
    "files": {
      "index.js": {
        "content": "import {createServer} from 'http';\ncreateServer((req, res) => { res.end('Hello World\n'); }).listen(3000);",
        "encoding": "utf-8"
      },
    }
  }
}
```

### Tailscale Client Metrics

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Explains how Tailscale collects and reports client metrics, providing insights into network performance, connection status, and usage patterns.

```APIDOC
Client Metrics:

Overview:
  Tailscale clients periodically send metrics to the Tailscale control server.
  These metrics help in monitoring network health and diagnosing issues.

Metrics Collected:
  - Connection status (connected, disconnected)
  - Latency and packet loss to peers
  - Bandwidth usage
  - Node uptime
  - Tailscale daemon version

Privacy:
  Tailscale is committed to user privacy. Metrics are anonymized where possible
  and do not include sensitive user data or traffic content.

Viewing Metrics:
  Client metrics are primarily used internally by Tailscale for operational purposes.
  Some high-level usage statistics might be available through the admin console.

```

### Set up Mastra AI SDK Agent with Code Execution

Source: https://context7_llms

Initializes the Mastra AI SDK agent and configures the LLM with the Freestyle code executor, enabling the agent to perform calculations and code-based tasks.

```ts
import { createMastra } from "@mastra/core";

const mastra = new Mastra();

const modelConfig: ModelConfig = {
  provider: "OPEN_AI",
  name: "gpt-4",
};

const llm = mastra.LLM(modelConfig);

const response = await llm.generate(
  "Calculate the sum of every number between 13 and 19 divided by the sum of every number between 8 and 13",
  {
    tools: {
      codeExecutor,
    },
  }
);
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Terminology and Concepts

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Defines key terms and concepts used within the Tailscale ecosystem to ensure a common understanding.

```APIDOC
Terminology and Concepts:

- **Tailnet**: Your private Tailscale network, connecting your devices.
- **Node**: Any device (server, laptop, phone) connected to your tailnet.
- **Control Plane**: The service responsible for authentication, coordination, and
  distributing configuration (e.g., WireGuard public keys, ACLs).
- **Data Plane**: The actual network traffic flowing between nodes, typically over WireGuard.
- **WireGuard**: The underlying VPN protocol used for secure, encrypted tunnels.
- **ACL (Access Control List)**: Policies defining which nodes can communicate with each other.
- **Tag**: A label used to group nodes for easier management in ACLs (e.g., `tag:prod-server`).
- **Subnet Router**: A node configured to route traffic between your tailnet and a private subnet.
- **Exit Node**: A node configured to route all internet traffic from other nodes in the tailnet.
- **Identity Provider (IdP)**: The service used for authenticating users (e.g., Google, Microsoft, GitHub).

```

--------------------------------

### Verify Domain

Source: https://context7_llms

Verifies a previously created domain verification request with Freestyle using Python. This confirms that the DNS record has been correctly set up.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

domain_verification_result = client.verify_domain("yourdomain.com")  # this also works for subdomains
if domain_verification_result.domain:
    print("Domain verified @ ", domain_verification_result.domain)
else:
    print("Domain verification failed", domain_verification_result.message)

```

### Gemini Python SDK Setup and Usage

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/code-execution/integrations/gemini

Demonstrates how to set up and use the Gemini Python SDK within the Freestyle environment. This includes initializing the SDK, configuring environment variables, and managing API keys.

```APIDOC
Gemini Python SDK:
  __init__(model_name: str, provider: str = 'gemini')
    model_name: The name of the Gemini model to use.
    provider: The provider to use (defaults to 'gemini').

  Configuration:
    - Environment Variables:
      - FREESTYLE_API_KEY: Your Freestyle API key.
      - GOOGLE_API_KEY: Your Google API key for Gemini.

  Usage Example:
    from freestyle import Freestyle

    # Initialize Freestyle with Gemini integration
    fs = Freestyle(provider='gemini')

    # Example of using a Gemini model for code execution
    result = fs.execute("print('Hello from Gemini!')")
    print(result)

  Dependencies:
    - google-generativeai
    - freestyle-python

  Notes:
    - Ensure your Freestyle API key and Google API key are set as environment variables.
    - Refer to the Freestyle documentation for advanced configuration options and other integrations.
```

### GitHub Synchronization Overview

Source: https://context7_llms

Explains the core functionalities of Freestyle's GitHub synchronization feature, including automatic syncing, leveraging GitHub workflows, collaboration, and conflict detection.

```markdown
# GitHub Synchronization

Freestyle provides seamless bidirectional synchronization between your Freestyle repositories and GitHub repositories. This integration allows you to maintain synchronized code across both platforms while leveraging Freestyle's infrastructure capabilities alongside GitHub's collaboration features.

## Overview

The GitHub sync feature enables you to:

- **Automatically sync changes** between Freestyle and GitHub repositories
- **Leverage GitHub workflows** on the Github side while using Freestyle's infrastructure
- **Collaborate on GitHub** your users' teams can continue to use Github without interruption while you utilize Freestyle's infrastructure
- **Avoid conflicts** with intelligent conflict detection
```

```javascript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const sandboxes = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: "your-api-key",
});

// Create a basic repository
sandboxes
  .createGitRepository({
    name: "example-repo",
```

--------------------------------

### OpenAI Function Calling to Tools Evolution

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Traces the evolution of tool integration in OpenAI models, from the early 'function-calling' in GPT-3.5-turbo to the more advanced 'tools' in GPT-4. This section highlights the limitations of early standards and the shift towards more complex tool definitions.

```APIDOC
OpenAI Function Calling and Tools:

GPT-3.5-turbo-0613 (June 2023):
  - Introduced `function-calling`.
  - Early, almost all first-party tools.
  - Examples: `send_email`, `get_current_weather`, `get_customers_by_revenue`, `extract_people_data`.
  - Limitations: Too limiting.

GPT-4:
  - Deprecated `functions` in favor of `tools`.
  - Allowed for more complex definitions.
  - Enabled domain-specific tasks with a series of tools.
  - Still largely first-party tools.
```

--------------------------------

### MCP Tutorials

Source: https://modelcontextprotocol.io/legacy/concepts/tools

Learn how to use MCP through various tutorials, including connecting to remote and local MCP servers, building MCP servers, and building MCP clients.

```markdown
Connect to Remote MCP Servers:
  Learn how to connect Claude to remote MCP servers and extend its capabilities with internet-hosted tools and data sources

Connect to Local MCP Servers:
  Learn how to extend Claude Desktop with local MCP servers to enable file system access and other powerful integrations

Build an MCP Server:
  Get started building your own server to use in Claude for Desktop and other clients.

Build an MCP Client:
  Get started building your own client that can integrate with all MCP servers.
```

### Authenticate Git CLI Operations

Source: https://context7_llms

Configures Git to use an access token for authentication with Freestyle domains, ensuring secure access to repositories.

```bash
# Set up credential helper for freestyle domains
git config --global credential.helper store
echo "https://x-access-token:your-token@git.freestyle.sh" >> ~/.git-credentials
```

--------------------------------

### Run Background Tasks

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Execute commands in the background using `process.exec` with the `true` or `background=True` argument. This allows other operations to proceed while the command runs.

```python
process.exec("npm run dev", background=True)
    # This will run in the background so you can continue doing other things
```

### Freestyle Git LLM Project Comparison

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Compares various source control methods including VM, Git on VM, S3 + DB, GitHub, and Freestyle Git across multiple features like version control, time travel, branching, permissions, and more.

```markdown
## All Together

Put together, depending on your needs and the scale of your application, you can choose from various source control methods. Below is a comparison table summarizing the strengths and weaknesses of each approach:

| Feature                  | VM              | Git on VM       | S3 + DB         | GitHub          | Freestyle Git  |
| ------------------------ | --------------- | --------------- | --------------- | --------------- | -------------- |
| Version Control          | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Time Travel              | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Branching/Forking        | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Fine-Grained Permissions | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Identity Management      | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck /> |
| Data Accessibility       | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| API Integration          | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| CI/CD Support            | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| Debuggability            | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <YellowTilde /> | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| Security                 | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Portability              | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Backup/Durability        | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck /> |
| Multi-Tenant Support     | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| Data Ownership           | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck />  | <GreenCheck />  | <RedX />        | <GreenCheck /> |
| Cost-Effectiveness       | <YellowTilde /> | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| Customization            | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck />  | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |
| GitHub Sync              | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | N/A             | <GreenCheck /> |
| Automation Triggers      | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <RedX />        | <YellowTilde /> | <GreenCheck /> |

We've built this API specifically for multi tenant apps, ensuring that it meets the unique needs of managing codebases on behalf of users and organizations. It provides a powerful and flexible solution for source control, enabling you to focus on building your AI applications without worrying about the underlying infrastructure.

If you're interested in trying it, you should read the [Using Git Guide](/git/git-overview)
```

--------------------------------

### Create Git Repository (Python)

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Creates a new Git repository on Freestyle using the Python SDK, optionally making it public for easier cloning during testing. This repository can then be used as a source for dev servers. It requires a name and a source URL.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

repo = client.create_repository(
  name="Test Repository from Python SDK",


  # This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.
  # The repo won't be listed on any public registry, but anybody
  # with the uuid can clone it. You should disable this in production.
  public=True,
  source=freestyle.CreateRepoSource.from_dict(
      {
          "type": "git",
          "url": "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn",
      }
  ),
)

print(f"Created repo with ID: {repo.repo_id}")

```

--------------------------------

### Create a Basic Git Repository

Source: https://context7_llms

Creates a new Git repository with a specified name. The repository ID is generated by Freestyle. The name is optional and for display purposes only.

```javascript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const sandboxes = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: "your-api-key",
});

// Create a basic repository
sandboxes
  .createGitRepository({
    name: "example-repo",
  })
  .then((res) => {
    console.log(res.repoId);
  });
```

### Code Executor with Environment Variables (Python)

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Configures the Freestyle code executor to provide environment variables to the execution context.

```python
import os
from freestyle.openai import execute_tool
import freestyle

(definition, runner) = freestyle.openai.execute_tool(
    os.environ.get("FREESTYLE_API_KEY"),
    freestyle.FreestyleExecuteScriptParamsConfiguration(
        envVars={"RESEND_API_KEY": os.environ.get("RESEND_API_KEY")}
        nodeModules={"resend":"4.1.2"}
    ),
  )
```

--------------------------------

### Freestyle.sh Git API Endpoints

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Provides details on the available API endpoints for interacting with Git objects. Includes methods for retrieving blobs, commits, trees, and tags.

```APIDOC
GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/blobs/{blobHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific blob from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - blobHash (string): The SHA hash of the blob.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a BlobObject.

GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/commits/{commitHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific commit from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - commitHash (string): The SHA hash of the commit.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a CommitObject.

GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/trees/{treeHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific tree from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - treeHash (string): The SHA hash of the tree.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a TreeObject.

GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/tags/{tagHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific tag from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - tagHash (string): The SHA hash of the tag.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a TagObject.
```

--------------------------------

### API Documentation - Core Functionality

Source: https://github.com/freestyle-sh/adorable

This section outlines the core API functionalities and their expected parameters and return values. It covers setup instructions and feature descriptions.

```APIDOC
Project Setup:
  - Dependencies:
    - Node.js
    - PostgreSQL database (Neon recommended)
    - Redis (for caching and session management)
    - Anthropic API key
    - Freestyle API key
    - Morph API key (optional)

Features:
  - Chat interface for interacting with AI code assistants
  - Patch-based code editing with user approval
  - Git integration for version control
  - Preview capabilities for code changes

API Endpoints (Conceptual):
  - /api/chat (POST): For interacting with the AI chat assistant.
    - Request Body:
      - message: string (The user's message)
      - conversationId: string (Optional, for continuing a conversation)
    - Response:
      - reply: string (AI's response)
      - conversationId: string (Updated conversation ID)

  - /api/code/patch (POST): For applying code patches.
    - Request Body:
      - patch: object (Details of the code patch)
      - approval: boolean (User's approval status)
    - Response:
      - status: string (Success or failure message)

  - /api/git/commit (POST): For committing code changes.
    - Request Body:
      - commitMessage: string
      - branch: string
    - Response:
      - status: string

  - /api/preview (GET): To get a preview of code changes.
    - Response:
      - previewUrl: string

```

--------------------------------

### Execute TypeScript Code

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Executes a TypeScript script using the Freestyle client. The script calculates the factorial of 543. The result is then logged to the console.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

const code = `export default () => {
// calculate the factorial of 543
return Array.from({ length: 543 }, (_, i) => i + 1).reduce((acc, cur) => acc * cur, 1);
}`;

api.executeScript(code).then((result) => {
console.log("Result: ", result);
});

```

--------------------------------

### Freestyle GitHub Integration Setup Process

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/git/github-sync

Details the step-by-step process for setting up Freestyle's GitHub integration. This includes creating a GitHub App, configuring webhooks, and understanding how the synchronization and conflict detection mechanisms work.

```APIDOC
Setup Process:
  Step 1: Create a GitHub App
    - Own a custom GitHub app with repository permissions for secure access.
  Step 2: Webhook Processing
    - Receive real-time notifications when code changes occur on GitHub or Freestyle.
  Step 3: Bidirectional Sync
    - Changes made on the GitHub repository are proactively synced to the Freestyle repository, and vice versa.
  Step 4: Conflict Detection
    - Prevents data loss by detecting diverged branches before applying changes.
```

### Deploy Next.js App (Python)

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Deploys a Next.js application from a GitHub repository to Freestyle using the Freestyle Python SDK. It configures the deployment with a specified domain and enables automatic code building.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

response = client.deploy_web(
    src=freestyle.DeploymentSource.from_dict(
    {
        "kind": "git",
        "url": "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn",
    }
    ),
    config=freestyle.FreestyleDeployWebConfiguration(
        domains=["welcomepython.style.dev"],
        build=freestyle.DeploymentBuildOptions.from_dict(True),
    ),
)


print(
    f"Deployed website @ {response.domains}"
)
```

### Create Git Repository

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Initializes a new Git repository for an AI App Builder chat. It requires an API key for authentication and allows specifying a repository name, visibility, and source URL. The `repoId` is crucial for referencing the code in subsequent operations.

```ts
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY,
});

const { repoId } = await freestyle.createGitRepository({
  name: "Test Repository",
  // This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.

    url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-next",
    type: "git",
  },
});
```

### Python Generative AI Setup and Usage

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/code-execution/integrations/gemini

This snippet demonstrates how to import libraries, initialize a generative AI client with an API key, and execute a tool. It covers setting up the environment variables for API keys and calling the `execute_tool` and `create` methods.

```python
from google.genai import types
import os
import freestyle.gemini

client = genai.Client(api_key=os.environ.get("GENERATIVEAI_API_KEY"))

definition, runner = freestyle.gemini.execute_tool(
    os.environ.get("FREESTYLE_API_KEY")
)

chat = client.chats.create()
```

### Deploying a Web Application with Domains

Source: https://context7_llms

Demonstrates how to deploy a web application using the Freestyle API, specifying a list of domains for the deployment. This action automatically creates domain mappings for each specified domain.

```typescript
import {
  Freestyle
} from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new Freestyle({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!,
});

async function deploy() {
  const result = await freestyle.deployWeb(
    {
      kind: "files",
      files: {
        /*...*/
      },
    },
    {
      domains: ["some.style.dev", "your.usersdomain.com"], // [!code ++] The domains here create domain mappings to the deployment
    }
  );
}
```

### Tailscale Traffic Security and Routing

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Information on securing internet activity using exit nodes and routing traffic through subnet routers to access resources on a network where the Tailscale client cannot be installed.

```APIDOC
Secure Traffic using Exit Nodes:
  - Designate devices in your tailnet as exit nodes to keep internet activity private on untrusted networks.
  - Configure tailnet devices to use these exit nodes.
  - Related Documentation:
    - Use exit nodes (quick guide): /kb/1408/quick-guide-exit-nodes
    - Exit nodes (main topic): /kb/1103/exit-nodes

Route Traffic using Subnets:
  - Use a subnet router to provide tailnet access to existing network resources, useful for devices like printers where the Tailscale client cannot be installed.
  - Related Documentation:
    - Configure a subnet router (quick guide): /kb/1406/quick-guide-subnets
    - Subnet routers (main topic): /kb/1019/subnets
```

### Execute Python Code

Source: https://context7_llms

Execute a Python script using the Freestyle client. The script calculates the factorial of 543. The result is printed to standard output.

```python
import freestyle
client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY") # make sure to set this

const code = """
export default () => {
// calculate the factorial of 543
return Array.from({ length: 543 }, (_, i) => i + 1).reduce((acc, cur) => acc * cur, 1);
}
"""

response = client.execute_script(code)

print(f"Result: {response.result}")

```

### Tailscale Webhooks

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Describes how to configure and use webhooks to receive real-time notifications from Tailscale about events occurring in your tailnet.

```APIDOC
Webhooks:

Purpose:
  Webhooks allow external services to subscribe to events within your Tailscale tailnet.
  When an event occurs, Tailscale sends an HTTP POST request to a specified URL.

Configuration:
  1. Go to the 'Settings' section of your Tailscale admin console.
  2. Navigate to the 'Webhooks' tab.
  3. Click 'Add webhook'.
  4. Enter the 'URL' where Tailscale should send notifications.
  5. Select the 'Events' you want to be notified about (e.g., device added, route approved).
  6. Click 'Save'.

Example Event Payload (Device Added):
  {
    "event": "device.create",
    "data": {
      "id": "device-id-123",
      "name": "new-laptop",
      "user": "user@example.com",
      "created": "2023-10-27T10:00:00Z"
    }
  }

```

### Combined Build Configuration

Source: https://context7_llms

Combines multiple build configuration options, including environment variables, a custom command, and an output directory, along with other deployment settings like entrypoint and domains.

```json
{
  "config": {
    "entrypoint": "index.js",
    "domains": ["yourdomain.com"],
    "envVars": {
      "API_KEY": "your-api-key",
      "SOME_OTHER_KEY": "some-other-value"
    },
    "build": {
      "envVars": {
        "ANOTHER_VAR": "another-value"
      },
      "command": "npm run build",
      "outDir": "dist"
    }
  }
}
```

### Serve Vite Dist Folder with Hono

TypeScript code using Hono to serve static files from the 'dist' directory. This is the entrypoint for a static Vite deployment.

```typescript
import { Hono } from "hono";
import { serveStatic } from "hono/deno";

const app = new Hono();

app.use("*", serveStatic({ root: "./dist" }));

Deno.serve(app.fetch);
```

### Device Management

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Covers operations related to managing devices within the Tailscale network, such as approval, renaming, and removal.

```APIDOC
Device Approval:
  Endpoint: /device/approve
  Method: POST
  Description: Approves a pending device for the network.
  Parameters:
    - deviceId (string): The unique identifier of the device to approve.
  Returns:
    - Success message or error.

Rename a Device:
  Endpoint: /device/{deviceId}/rename
  Method: PUT
  Description: Renames an existing device on the network.
  Parameters:
    - deviceId (string): The unique identifier of the device to rename.
    - newName (string): The new desired name for the device.
  Returns:
    - Success message or error.

Remove a Device:
  Endpoint: /device/{deviceId}/remove
  Method: DELETE
  Description: Removes a device from the Tailscale network.
  Parameters:
    - deviceId (string): The unique identifier of the device to remove.
  Returns:
    - Success message or error.
```

### Vercel AI SDK Agent Setup

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/code-execution/integrations/vercel

This section details the process of setting up a Vercel AI SDK agent to leverage code execution. It includes installing necessary dependencies, configuring the code executor, and integrating it with the agent.

```typescript
import { Agent } from '@vercel/ai';
import { CodeExecutor } from './code-executor'; // Assuming CodeExecutor is defined elsewhere

const executor = new CodeExecutor();

const agent = new Agent({
  // ... other agent configurations
  tools: [
    executor.getToolDefinition(), // Assuming CodeExecutor has a method to get its tool definition
  ],
});

// Example usage of the agent with code execution
agent.run('Execute the following Python code: print("Hello, World!")');
```

### Freestyle.sh Git API Endpoints

Source: https://context7_llms

Provides details on the available API endpoints for interacting with Git objects. Includes methods for retrieving blobs, commits, trees, and tags.

```APIDOC
GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/blobs/{blobHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific blob from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - blobHash (string): The SHA hash of the blob.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a BlobObject.

GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/commits/{commitHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific commit from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - commitHash (string): The SHA hash of the commit.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a CommitObject.

GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/trees/{treeHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific tree from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - treeHash (string): The SHA hash of the tree.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a TreeObject.

GET /git/v1/repo/{repoId}/git/tags/{tagHash}
  Description: Retrieves a specific tag from the repository.
  Parameters:
    - repoId (string): The ID of the repository.
    - tagHash (string): The SHA hash of the tag.
  Responses:
    200 OK: Returns a TagObject.
```

### Get Commit Author and Date

```shell

# Example Output:
# John Doe <john.doe@example.com> 2023-10-27T10:30:00-07:00
```

### OpenAI Function Calling to Tools Evolution

Source: https://context7_llms

Traces the evolution of tool integration in OpenAI models, from the early 'function-calling' in GPT-3.5-turbo to the more advanced 'tools' in GPT-4. This section highlights the limitations of early standards and the shift towards more complex tool definitions.

```APIDOC
OpenAI Function Calling and Tools:

GPT-3.5-turbo-0613 (June 2023):
  - Introduced `function-calling`.
  - Early, almost all first-party tools.
  - Examples: `send_email`, `get_current_weather`, `get_customers_by_revenue`, `extract_people_data`.
  - Limitations: Too limiting.

GPT-4:
  - Deprecated `functions` in favor of `tools`.
  - Allowed for more complex definitions.
  - Enabled domain-specific tasks with a series of tools.
  - Still largely first-party tools.
```

```APIDOC
Invite-Only Features:

Overview:
  Tailscale occasionally offers early access to new features through an invite-only program.
  This allows for focused testing and feedback before a general release.

Examples of Past Invite-Only Features:
  - Tailscale SSH (now generally available)
  - Specific advanced policy features

How to Get Access:
  - Keep an eye on the Tailscale blog and community forums for announcements
    regarding new invite-only programs.
  - Follow Tailscale on social media for updates.
  - Some features might require direct contact with the Tailscale team for consideration.

```

### Next.js Deployment Example

Source: https://freestyle.sh/

Example of deploying a Next.js application using Freestyle. This demonstrates the ease of integrating with popular frameworks.

```javascript
import freestyle from 'freestyle-sdk';

async function deployNextApp() {
  const deployment = await freestyle.deployments.create({
    framework: 'nextjs',
    repositoryUrl: 'https://github.com/your-username/your-nextjs-app',
    branch: 'main'
  });
  console.log('Next.js app deployed:', deployment.url);
}
```

### Deploy Web Application from Git

Source: https://context7_llms

Deploys a web application directly from a Git repository. Supports specifying the source repository URL, branch, entrypoint, domains, and enables automatic building.

```javascript
// TODO: This is not yet implemented
// Deploy a web application from a Git repository
const yourRepoId = "your-repo-id";

sandboxes
  .deployWeb({
    source: {
      type: "git",
      url: `https://git.freestyle.sh/${yourRepoId}`,
      branch: "main", // Optional: defaults to main
    },
    {
      entrypoint: "index.js", // Optional: defaults to index.js
      domains: ["example.style.dev"], // Optional: specify domains
      build: true // automatically detect your framework and build for you
    }
  })
  .then((deployment) => {
    console.log(`Deployed to: ${deployment.url}`);
  });
```

### Create Git Repository

Source: https://context7_llms

Creates a Git repository on Freestyle using the Python SDK. This repository can be used as a base for dev servers and can be configured as public for easier cloning during testing. It supports cloning from a specified Git URL.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

repo = client.create_repository(
  name="Test Repository from Python SDK",


  # This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.
  # The repo won't be listed on any public registry, but anybody
  # with the uuid can clone it. You should disable this in production.
  public=True,
  source=freestyle.CreateRepoSource.from_dict(
      {
          "type": "git",
          "url": "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn",
      }
  ),
)

print(f"Created repo with ID: {repo.repo_id}")

```

Source: https://context7_llms

Configures the Freestyle code executor to include specific Node.js modules for code execution.

```python
import os
from freestyle.openai import execute_tool
import freestyle

(definition, runner) = freestyle.openai.execute_tool(
    os.environ.get("FREESTYLE_API_KEY"),
    freestyle.FreestyleExecuteScriptParamsConfiguration(
        nodeModules={"mathjs": "14.3.1"}
    ),
  )
```

### Tailscale CLI Commands

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

This section details common Tailscale command-line interface (CLI) commands for managing your Tailscale network. It covers commands for connecting, disconnecting, and configuring Tailscale clients.

```APIDOC
tailscale up
  - Starts and connects Tailscale to your network.

tailscale down
  - Disconnects Tailscale from your network.

tailscale status
  - Shows the current status of your Tailscale connection.

tailscale serve
  - Enables the Tailscale serve feature for sharing files.

tailscale funnel
  - Manages Tailscale Funnel for exposing services publicly.

tailscale lock
  - Manages Tailscale Lock for device authentication.

tailscaled
  - The background daemon for Tailscale.
```

### Deploy Vite App via API

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

TypeScript code to deploy a Vite application using the Freestyle API client. It prepares the directory and specifies the entrypoint and domains.

```ts
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";
import { prepareDirForDeploymentSync } from "freestyle-sandboxes/utils";

// Create a sandboxes client
const sandboxes = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!,
});

async function deploy() {
  await sandboxes.deployWeb(prepareDirForDeploymentSync("."), {
    entrypoint: "main.ts",
    // put whatever domains you want here
    domains: ["example.style.dev"],
  });
}

deploy();
```

### MCP Server Configuration

Source: https://code.visualstudio.com/docs/copilot/chat/mcp-servers

An example configuration file (.vscode/mcp.json) for setting up MCP servers. It demonstrates defining inputs for API keys and configuring different server types like Docker-based Perplexity, GitHub Copilot, and a fetch server.

```json
{
  "inputs": [
    {
      "type": "promptString",
      "id": "perplexity-key",
      "description": "Perplexity API Key",
      "password": true
    }
  ],
  "servers": {
    "Perplexity": {
      "type": "stdio",
      "command": "docker",
      "args": ["run", "-i", "--rm", "-e", "PERPLEXITY_API_KEY", "mcp/perplexity-ask"],
      "env": {
        "PERPLEXITY_API_KEY": "${input:perplexity-key}"
      }
    },
    "Github": {
      "url": "https://api.githubcopilot.com/mcp/"
    },
    "fetch": {
      "type": "stdio",
      "command": "uvx",
      "args": ["mcp-server-fetch"]
    }
  }
}
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Key Prefixes

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Explains the different key prefixes used by Tailscale, which indicate the type and purpose of authentication keys.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Key Prefixes:

  Purpose:
    Key prefixes help identify the type and capabilities of Tailscale authentication keys.

  Common Prefixes:
    - `tskey-auth-`: Standard authentication keys used for nodes joining the tailnet.
    - `tskey-cert-`: Keys used for certificate issuance, often related to Tailscale SSH.
    - `tskey-tailnet-`: Keys related to tailnet-level operations or administration.
    - `tskey-user-`: Keys associated with user accounts.

  Key Usage:
    When using keys with commands like `tailscale up`, the prefix helps Tailscale understand the key's intended use.

  Example:
    `tailscale up --authkey=tskey-auth-xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx`

  Security Considerations:
    Treat all keys as sensitive information.
```

### API Request Examples

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/API-Reference/web/handle_deploy_web_v2

Provides examples of how to make API requests using cURL and JavaScript.

```cURL
curl -X POST <your_api_endpoint> \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{ "message": "Hello, world!", "entrypoint": "chat" }'
```

```JavaScript
fetch('<your_api_endpoint>', {
  method: 'POST',
  headers: {
    'Content-Type': 'application/json'
  },
  body: JSON.stringify({
    message: 'Hello, world!',
    entrypoint: 'chat'
  })
})
.then(response => response.json())
.then(data => console.log(data));
```

### Deploy Next.js App (TypeScript)

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Deploys a Next.js application from a GitHub repository to Freestyle using the Freestyle Sandboxes SDK. It configures the deployment with a specified domain and enables automatic code building.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

api
  .deployWeb(
    {
      kind: "git",
      url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn", // URL of the repository you want to deploy
    },
    {
      domains: ["yourtestdomain.style.dev"],
      build: true, // automatically detects the framework and builds the code
    }
  )
  .then((result) => {
    console.log("Deployed website @ ", result.domains);
  });
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Serve Configuration

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Guidance on using Tailscale Serve to share files or directories directly from your devices. This feature allows for simple, secure file sharing within your tailnet.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Serve:

  Purpose:
    Tailscale Serve allows you to share files or directories from your device securely over Tailscale.

  Usage:
    `tailscale serve <directory> [--port <port>] [--advertise]`

    - `<directory>`: The directory to share.
    - `--port <port>`: (Optional) The port to serve on. Defaults to 8080.
    - `--advertise`: (Optional) Advertise this service using Tailscale's service discovery.

  Example:
    To share the current directory on port 8080:
    `tailscale serve .`

    To share a specific directory and advertise it:
    `tailscale serve /path/to/files --advertise`

  Accessing Shared Content:
    You can access the shared content using the Tailscale IP address of the serving device and the specified port, or via the advertised service name if applicable.
```

```APIDOC
Freestyle Git API:
```

### Create Git Repository

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Creates a new Git repository on Freestyle, optionally making it public for easier cloning during testing. This repository can then be used as a source for dev servers. It requires a name and a source URL.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes();


const { repoId } = await freestyle.createGitRepository({
  name: "Test Repository",

  // This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.
  // The repo won't be listed on any public registry, but anybody
  // with the uuid can clone it. You should disable this in production.
  public: true,

  source: {
    url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-next",
    type: "git",
  },
});

console.log(`Created repo with ID: ${repoId}`);

```

### Local Development Webhook Setup with Tailscale

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/git/git-overview

Instructions for setting up a local development environment to receive Git trigger webhook events using Tailscale. This involves installing Tailscale, creating a secure tunnel, and using the provided Tailscale URL as the webhook endpoint.

```javascript
# Install Tailscale (if not already installed)
# Follow the quickstart guide: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

# Expose your local server (e.g., running on port 3000)
tailscale funnel 3000

# Example Output:
# Available on the internet:
# 
# https://<device name>.<tailnet id/name>.ts.net/
# |-- proxy http://127.0.0.1:3000
# 
# Press Ctrl+C to exit.

# Use the provided URL as the webhook URL in your trigger configuration.
```

--------------------------------

### Create Chat Repository and Request Dev Server

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

This function initializes Freestyle Sandboxes, creates a new Git repository from a template, and requests a development server for it. It requires an API key for Freestyle Sandboxes and returns the repository ID and ephemeral URL.

```ts
import {
  FreestyleSandboxes,
} from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!,
});

export async function createChat() {
  const { repoId } = await freestyle.createGitRepository({
    name: "Test Repository",
    public: true,
    source: {
      url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-next", // [!code highlight] replace this with your own template repo
      type: "git",
    },
  });

  const { ephemeralUrl, mcpEphemeralUrl } = await freestyle.requestDevServer({
    repoId: repoId,
  });

  return {
    repoId,
    ephemeralUrl,
  };
}
```

--------------------------------

### Tree Object Structure

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Defines the structure of a Tree object. It contains an array of entries, each specifying the type (blob/tree), path, and SHA hash.

```typescript
interface TreeObject {
  // The tree's entries (files and subdirectories)
  tree: Array<{
    // The entry's type: "blob" (file) or "tree" (directory)
    type: "blob" | "tree";
    // The entry's path (filename or directory name)
    path: string;
    // The entry's hash
    sha: string;
  }>;
  // The tree's hash
  sha: string;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Webhooks

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Documentation on setting up and using Tailscale webhooks to receive real-time notifications about events occurring within your tailnet, such as node changes or policy updates.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Webhooks:

  Purpose:
    Webhooks allow external applications to receive real-time event notifications from Tailscale.

  Configuring Webhooks:
    Webhooks are configured in the Tailscale admin console under the "Webhooks" or "Events" section.

  Event Types:
    Tailscale can send notifications for various events, including:
    - Node added/removed/changed.
    - Policy changes.
    - User invitations/changes.
    - Key expirations.

  Webhook URL:
    You need to provide a publicly accessible URL (HTTPS) where Tailscale will send the event data (payload).

  Payload Format:
    Event data is typically sent as a JSON payload.

  Security:
    Consider securing your webhook endpoint using shared secrets or other authentication methods to verify the source of the events.
```

--------------------------------

### Deploy Web Action

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

A server action to deploy a web application by referencing its Git repository. It takes a repository ID and a list of domains to deploy to, utilizing the FreestyleSandboxes service.

```ts
"use server";
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY,
});

export async function deployAction(
  repoId: string, // [!code highlight] the repoId for your app
  domains: string[] // [!code highlight] the domains you want to deploy to
) {
  const { domains } = await freestyle.deployWeb(
    {
      kind: "git",
      repoUrl: `https://git.freestyle.sh/${repoId}`,
    },
    {
      domains,
      envVars: {
        // ... any environment variables you want to set
      },
    }
  );
}
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Policy File Syntax

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Defines the syntax and structure for creating Tailscale policy files, which are used to control access between devices in your tailnet.

```APIDOC
Policy File Syntax:

// Define groups of users or devices
group tailscale {
  "user1@example.com",
  "user2@example.com",
}

group servers {
  tag:tag:server,
}

// Define network ACLs
"group:tailscale" -> "group:servers": 80, 443;

// Allow all traffic within the tailnet
"group:self" -> "group:self": accept;

// Deny all other traffic by default
"*" -> "*": deny;

// Example of routing specific subnets
"group:tailscale" -> "tag:subnet-router": 10.0.0.0/8;

// Example of allowing SSH access from specific users to specific servers
"user:admin@example.com" -> "tag:webserver": 22;

```

### Run Background Tasks

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Execute commands in the background using `process.exec` with the `true` or `background=True` argument. This allows other operations to proceed while the command runs.

```typescript
await process.exec("npm run dev", true);
    // This will run in the background so you can continue doing other things
```

### DNS Configuration for Domain Mapping

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Provides DNS record configurations for mapping domains to Freestyle deployments. This includes settings for single APEX domains, subdomains, and wildcard subdomains.

```APIDOC
APIDOC:
  Domain Mapping:
    Single APEX Domain (e.g., yourdomain.com):
      Type: A
      NAME: @
      VALUE: 35.235.84.134

    Subdomain (e.g., subdomain.yourdomain.com):
      Type: A
      NAME: subdomain
      VALUE: 35.235.84.134

    All Subdomains (e.g., *.yourdomain.com):
      Type: A
      NAME: *
      VALUE: 35.235.84.134

    Verification Note:
      Use `dig domain.youexpect.com` to test DNS record correctness.
```

```typescript
await fs.writeFile("src/index.tsx", `console.log("Hello World!");`);
```

--------------------------------

### MCP for Tool Sharing

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Explains how MCP (Model Context Protocol) revolutionized tool sharing among AI metaframeworks and models. Before MCP, sharing code executors required individual packages for each integration, which was cumbersome. MCP provides a standard for easy tool sharing.

```English
Before MCP existed, Freestyle wanted to share our code executor with other companies, so in order to share it we were forced to create individual packages for [every AI Metaframework and model we wanted to support](/code-execution/integrations/vercel) — this sucked, which is why most companies didn't bother, a few did.

In November 2024, [MCP](https://www.anthropic.com/news/model-context-protocol) changed this, creating a standard that makes it easy for any team to share tools with agents, and for any agent to use them.
```

### Execute Script with Custom Environment Variables

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Shows how to execute a script in a Freestyle sandbox with custom environment variables. These variables are accessible within the script via `process.env`.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

api
  .executeScript(`return process.env.SOME_ENV_VAR;`, {
    envVars: {
      SOME_ENV_VAR: "Hello, World!",
    },
  })
  .then((result) => {
    console.log("Result: ", result);
  });
```

### Create Git Repository

Source: https://context7_llms

Creates a Git repository on Freestyle, which can be used as a base for dev servers. The repository can be made public for easier cloning during testing. It supports cloning from a specified Git URL.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes();


const { repoId } = await freestyle.createGitRepository({
  name: "Test Repository",

  // This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.
  // The repo won't be listed on any public registry, but anybody
  // with the uuid can clone it. You should disable this in production.
  public: true,

  source: {
    url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-next",
    type: "git",
  },
});

console.log(`Created repo with ID: ${repoId}`);

```

```typescript
interface TreeObject {
```

### Create Repository and Request Dev Server

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/dev-servers/dev-servers

Demonstrates how to create a new repository using the Freestyle SDK and then request a development server for that repository. The `repoId` obtained from creation is used to provision the dev server.

```typescript
import { FreestyleBase } from "freestyle-base";

const freestyle = new FreestyleBase();

const repo = await freestyle.createRepo({
    name: "my-new-repo",
    description: "A repo created with the Freestyle SDK",
    private: false,
});

console.log(`Created repo with ID: ${repo.repo_id}`);

// Then, you can request a dev server for the repo you just created.
const devServer = await freestyle.requestDevServer({ repoId: repo.repo_id });

console.log(`Dev Server URL: ${devServer.ephemeralUrl}`);
```

### Execute TypeScript Code

Source: https://context7_llms

Execute a TypeScript script using the Freestyle client. The script calculates the factorial of 543. Results are logged to the console.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

const code = `export default () => {
// calculate the factorial of 543
return Array.from({ length: 543 }, (_, i) => i + 1).reduce((acc, cur) => acc * cur, 1);
}`;

api.executeScript(code).then((result) => {
console.log("Result: ", result);
});

```

### Authenticate Git CLI with Freestyle

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Configures Git credentials to authenticate with Freestyle domains using an access token. It involves setting a global credential helper and storing the token in the git-credentials file.

```bash
# Set up credential helper for freestyle domains
git config --global credential.helper store
echo "https://x-access-token:your-token@git.freestyle.sh" >> ~/.git-credentials
```

### Create Domain Verification Request

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Creates a domain verification request with Freestyle. This process involves generating a verification code that needs to be added as a TXT DNS record for the domain.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

const domainVerificationRequset = api.createDomainVerificationRequest("yourdomain.com") // this also works for subdomains
  .then((result) => {
    console.log("Domain verification request created @ ", result);
    /* The result looks like: { 
      verificationCode: string;
      domain: string;
    } */
  });

```

### Deploy Website with Python

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/web/web

Deploys a website from a Git repository to Freestyle using the 'freestyle' Python library. This example configures the deployment with a custom domain and enables automatic framework detection and building.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

response = client.deploy_web(
    src=freestyle.DeploymentSource.from_dict(
    {
        "kind": "git",
        "url": "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn",
    }
    ),
    config=freestyle.FreestyleDeployWebConfiguration(
        domains=["welcomepython.style.dev"],
        build=freestyle.DeploymentBuildOptions.from_dict(True),
    ),
)


print(
    f"Deployed website @ {response.domains}"
)
```

### Configure Gemini Code Executor with Node Modules

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Sets up the Freestyle code executor for Gemini, including specific Node.js modules for execution. This allows the AI code to utilize external libraries like `mathjs`.

```python
import os
import freestyle.gemini
import freestyle

definition, runner = freestyle.gemini.execute_tool(
    os.environ.get("FREESTYLE_API_KEY"),
    freestyle.FreestyleExecuteScriptParamsConfiguration(
        nodeModules={"mathjs": "14.3.1"}
    ),
  )
```

### Tailscale API - OAuth Clients

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Documentation for managing OAuth clients within the Tailscale API. This allows for integration with third-party applications.

```APIDOC
API: OAuth Clients

Endpoint: /oauth/clients

GET /oauth/clients
  Description: Lists all OAuth clients for the authenticated user.
  Parameters:
    None
  Returns:
    An array of OAuth client objects, each containing:
      - id: Unique identifier for the client
      - name: Name of the OAuth client
      - redirect_uris: List of allowed redirect URIs
      - created_at: Timestamp of creation

POST /oauth/clients
  Description: Creates a new OAuth client.
  Parameters:
    name (string, required): The name for the new OAuth client.
    redirect_uris (array of strings, required): Allowed URIs for redirection after authentication.
  Returns:
    The newly created OAuth client object.

GET /oauth/clients/{client_id}
  Description: Retrieves details of a specific OAuth client.
  Parameters:
    client_id (string, required): The ID of the OAuth client to retrieve.
  Returns:
    The OAuth client object.

PUT /oauth/clients/{client_id}
  Description: Updates an existing OAuth client.
  Parameters:
    client_id (string, required): The ID of the OAuth client to update.
    name (string, optional): The new name for the OAuth client.
    redirect_uris (array of strings, optional): The updated list of allowed redirect URIs.
  Returns:
    The updated OAuth client object.

DELETE /oauth/clients/{client_id}
  Description: Deletes an OAuth client.
  Parameters:
    client_id (string, required): The ID of the OAuth client to delete.
  Returns:
    Success message or status code.
```

### Freestyle AI Upcoming Features

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

This section details the planned features and development progress for Freestyle AI. It includes items that are completed, in progress, or cancelled, providing a roadmap for future enhancements.

```markdown
- [x] **Usage/Metrics**: We are working on generalized metrics for all our API
- [ ] **Usage/Metrics V2**: We are working on more granular metrics for all our APIs, including specific domain, user and deployment tracking. We're also examining the concept of script injection for granular metrics on your user's behavior across the apps you deploy.

- [x] **Git Triggers**: We are working on Git triggers to allow you to run code actions are taken on a Git repository you manage
- [x] **Python SDK**: We are working on a Python SDK to allow you to interact with Freestyle from Python more easily (Released, feature incomplete)
- [ ] **Better DNS**: We are working on improvements to our DNS API to make it more powerful, support more record types, be easier to delete records and have a UI in our Dashboard

- [ ] ~~**Hot Module Replacement**: We are working on a Serverless HMR solution to give instant deploys for those who can't wait for builds~~ (Cancelled in favor of dev servers)
- [ ] ~~**Firecracker Service**: We are working on a Firecracker service to give you the ability to run Firecrackers on your users behalf~~ (Cancelled in favor of dev servers)
- [x] **Dev Servers**: New service to run development servers, display their previews to your users, and give your AI Access to control them.
- [ ] **Dev Servers Computer Use**: We've already shipped chromium into our dev servers, making them prepared to run your playwright in VM without any external services, but we're beta testing adding a pre-built computer use tool for our customers to be able to let their AI try their apps in dev.
- [ ] **Dev Server File System Decoupling**: Running dev servers is expensive, we're working to decouple the filesystem from the dev server so you can read/write from it without starting the machine — this will mean you don't have to start the server until your AI is done generating code, saving you a lot of compute hours and money.
- [ ] **Dev Server Stingy Mode**: This is a dev server mode we're working on to exponentially cut down on your dev server costs. We're not sharing too much about it yet, but its going to mean you only pay for the compute you use — think serverless dev servers.

- [ ] **Freestyle MCP**: We're working on Freestyle Cloud MCP to allow your AI to pull your debug logs and help you build with Freestyle more easily.
```

```markdown
## Deploying Vite Projects
```

--------------------------------

### Commit Object Structure

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Defines the structure of a Commit object. Includes author, committer, message, tree information, parent commits, and the commit SHA.

```typescript
interface CommitObject {
  // The commit author
  author: {
    date: string;
    name: string;
    email: string;
  };
  // The committer (may be different from author)
  committer: {
    date: string;
    name: string;
    email: string;
  };
  // The commit message
  message: string;
  // The tree this commit points to
  tree: {
    sha: string;
  };
  // Parent commits (usually one, multiple for merge commits)
  parents: Array<{
    sha: string;
  }>;
  // The commit's hash
  sha: string;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Execute Script with Custom Environment Variables

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Shows how to execute a script in a Freestyle sandbox using Python with custom environment variables. These variables are accessible within the script via `process.env`.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

result = client.execute_script(
    code="""
    return process.env.SOME_ENV_VAR;
    """,
    freestyle.FreestyleExecuteScriptParamsConfiguration(
        env_vars={
            "SOME_ENV_VAR": "Hello, World!"
        }
    )
)

print(f"Result: {result.result}")
```

### Tailscale Client Metrics

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Information regarding the collection and usage of client metrics by Tailscale. These metrics help improve the service and diagnose potential issues.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Client Metrics:

  Purpose:
    Client metrics provide insights into the performance and health of Tailscale clients, helping to identify and resolve issues.

  Data Collected:
    Metrics may include connection statistics, performance data, error reports, and usage patterns.

  Privacy:
    Tailscale emphasizes privacy and typically anonymizes or aggregates metrics data.

  Enabling/Disabling Metrics:
    Users can usually control whether client metrics are shared via the Tailscale client settings or the admin console.

  Usage:
    The collected metrics are used by Tailscale to:
    - Improve performance and reliability.
    - Debug and fix bugs.
    - Understand usage patterns to guide future development.
```

### Request Dev Server (Python)

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Requests a dev server instance for a given repository ID using the Python SDK. The dev server will automatically run 'npm run dev' and will shut down if not kept alive. It provides an ephemeral URL for accessing the running application.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

dev_server = client.request_dev_server(repo_id=repo.repo_id)

print(f"Dev Server URL: {dev_server.ephemeral_url}")

```

### Device Management and MagicDNS

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

This section details how to manage devices within your Tailscale network, including renaming them for better organization and utilizing MagicDNS for simplified host communication.

```markdown
Every device added to a tailnet, including servers, nodes, phones, and personal computers is assigned a unique name generated from the device's OS hostname. This name is displayed in the [**Machines**](https://login.tailscale.com/admin/machines) page of the admin console. You can also [rename a device](/kb/1098/machine-names#renaming-a-machine) to help you locate and organize devices in the **Machines** page list.

[MagicDNS](/kb/1081/magicdns) makes communicating with devices across your tailnet easier by allowing you to use the name listed in the **Machines** page of the admin console instead of an IP address. This works using automatically assigned OS hostnames or renamed device names. MagicDNS is enabled by default, and we recommend you keep it enabled.
```

--------------------------------

### GitHub Sync Configuration API Reference

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Provides details on configuring GitHub synchronization programmatically via the API. This includes the endpoint and parameters required for setting up the sync between Freestyle and GitHub repositories. Note that the Python SDK does not yet support this functionality.

```APIDOC
Endpoint: /API-Reference/git/configure_github_sync

Method: POST (or relevant HTTP method)

Description: Configures bidirectional synchronization between a Freestyle repository and a GitHub repository.

Parameters:
  repoId (string): The unique identifier for the Freestyle repository.
  githubRepoName (string): The full name of the GitHub repository in the format 'owner/repository-name'.

Prerequisites:
  - The GitHub App must be installed on the specified GitHub repository.
  - The user or service account making the API call must have the necessary permissions.

Example Usage (Conceptual):
POST /API-Reference/git/configure_github_sync
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "repoId": "your-freestyle-repo-id",
  "githubRepoName": "user/repo-name"
}

Response:
  - Success: 200 OK or 201 Created with confirmation.
  - Error: 400 Bad Request (e.g., invalid repoId, repo not found), 403 Forbidden (e.g., insufficient permissions), 404 Not Found (e.g., GitHub repository not found).

Related Information:
  - Freestyle SDKs (JavaScript supports this, Python does not yet).
  - Admin Dashboard for manual configuration and status monitoring.
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Funnel Configuration

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Instructions for setting up Tailscale Funnel, which allows you to expose a service running on your tailnet to the public internet securely. This involves enabling Funnel and configuring which services to expose.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Funnel:

  Enabling Funnel:
    Tailscale Funnel is enabled via the admin console under the "Funnel" settings.

  Exposing Services:
    Once enabled, you can expose services by running `tailscale funnel <port>` on the node hosting the service.

    Example:
      To expose a web server running on port 80:
      `tailscale funnel 80`

  Public URL:
    Tailscale Funnel provides a public URL (e.g., `https://<node-name>.<tailnet-name>.ts.net`) for the exposed service.

  HTTPS Certificates:
    Tailscale automatically provisions and manages HTTPS certificates for Funnel endpoints.

  Limitations:
    - Funnel is designed for HTTP/HTTPS traffic.
    - It is not suitable for all types of services.
    - Check Tailscale documentation for current limitations and best practices.
```

--------------------------------

### GitHub Synchronization Architecture

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Details the technical architecture behind Freestyle's GitHub integration, including the role of GitHub Apps, webhook processing, bidirectional sync, and conflict detection mechanisms.

```markdown
## How It Works

Freestyle's GitHub integration uses GitHub Apps to provide secure, repository-specific access. When you push code to either platform, changes are automatically synchronized to the other, ensuring both repositories stay in sync.

### Architecture

1. **GitHub App**: You own the custom Github app with repository permissions for secure access to the repositories on Github
2. **Webhook Processing**: You get real-time notifications when code changes occur on Github or on Freestyle
3. **Bidirectional Sync**: When a change is made on the Github repository, its proactively synced to the Freestyle repository, and vice versa
4. **Conflict Detection**: We prevents data loss by detecting diverged branches before applying changes
```

--------------------------------

### Create Git Repository

Source: https://context7_llms

Initializes a new Git repository for an AI App Builder chat. It requires an API key for authentication and allows specifying a repository name, visibility, and source URL. The `repoId` is crucial for referencing the code in subsequent operations.

```ts
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY,
});

const { repoId } = await freestyle.createGitRepository({
  name: "Test Repository",
  // This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.
  public: true,
  source: {
    url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-next",
    type: "git",
  },
});
```

### Deploy Next.js App (Python)

Source: https://context7_llms

Deploys a Next.js application from a GitHub repository to Freestyle using the Freestyle Python SDK. It configures the deployment with a specified domain and enables automatic code building.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

response = client.deploy_web(
    src=freestyle.DeploymentSource.from_dict(
    {
        "kind": "git",
        "url": "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn",
    }
    ),
    config=freestyle.FreestyleDeployWebConfiguration(
        domains=["welcomepython.style.dev"],
        build=freestyle.DeploymentBuildOptions.from_dict(True),
    ),
)


print(
    f"Deployed website @ {response.domains}"
)
```

### Tailscale Log Streaming

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Information on configuring Tailscale to stream logs to external systems for centralized logging and analysis.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Log Streaming:

  Purpose:
    Allows you to forward Tailscale logs (client logs, audit logs, etc.) to external log management systems for centralized analysis and retention.

  Integration Methods:
    - **Webhooks**: Configure Tailscale webhooks to send event data to your logging endpoint.
    - **Log Forwarding Agents**: Use agents like Fluentd, Logstash, or Vector on your nodes to collect and forward Tailscale logs.
    - **Direct API Access**: Potentially use Tailscale's API to retrieve logs programmatically.

  Common Destinations:
    - SIEM systems (e.g., Splunk, ELK Stack).
    - Cloud logging services (e.g., AWS CloudWatch, Google Cloud Logging).
    - Centralized log aggregation platforms.

  Configuration:
    Configuration typically involves setting up the destination endpoint and specifying which logs to stream in the Tailscale admin console or via configuration files.
```

### JavaScript SDK Usage

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/API-Reference/git/configure_github_sync

Example of how to use the Freestyle Sandboxes JavaScript SDK to list domains. Ensure you have the 'freestyle-sandboxes' package installed and replace 'your-api-key' with your actual API key.

```javascript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from 'freestyle-sandboxes';

const sandboxes = new FreestyleSandboxes({
 apiKey: 'your-api-key',
});

sandboxes.listDomains().then((response) => {
 console.log(response);
});
```

### Python LLM Integration Example

Source: https://www.typescriptlang.org/

This Python code snippet illustrates how to integrate with a Large Language Model (LLM) using a common library like OpenAI's Python client. It covers initializing the client, making a completion request, and handling the response. Ensure you have the 'openai' library installed (`pip install openai`) and your API key configured.

```python
import openai

# Ensure your OpenAI API key is set as an environment variable
# export OPENAI_API_KEY='your-api-key'

# Initialize the OpenAI client
client = openai.OpenAI()

# Define the prompt and model
prompt_text = "What is the capital of France?"
model_name = "gpt-3.5-turbo"

try:
    # Make a completion request
    response = client.chat.completions.create(
        model=model_name,
        messages=[
            {"role": "system", "content": "You are a helpful assistant."},
            {"role": "user", "content": prompt_text}
        ]
    )

    # Extract and print the response content
    if response.choices:
        print(response.choices[0].message.content)
    else:
        print("No response generated.")

except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")

```

### Hono Server for Static Assets

Source: https://context7_llms

A simple Hono server implementation in TypeScript for Deno that serves static files. It's configured to serve from a './static' directory and provides a fallback to './static/index.html' for root requests.

```typescript
import { Hono } from "hono";
import { serveStatic } from "hono/deno";

const app = new Hono();

app.use("*", serveStatic({ root: "./static" }));

// fallback to index.html
app.get("*", serveStatic({ path: "./static/index.html" }));

Deno.serve(app.fetch);
```

### Execute Script with Custom Node Modules

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Demonstrates how to execute a script in a Freestyle sandbox using Python, specifying custom Node.js modules and their versions. This allows for the use of external libraries like 'axios' to interact with external APIs.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

result = client.execute_script(
    code="""

    import axios from 'axios';

    export default async () => {
        // Fetch data from an external API
        const res = await axios.get('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/todos/1');
        return res.data;
    }
    """,
    freestyle.FreestyleExecuteScriptParamsConfiguration(
      node_modules={
        "axios": "0.21.1"  # specify the version of the module you want to use
      }
    )
  ),
)
print(f"Result: {result.result}")
```

### Manage Git Repository Permissions

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Manages permissions for Git identities on repositories. You can grant read or write access, list existing permissions, and revoke access.

```javascript
// Grant read-only access
sandboxes
  .grantPermission({
    identityId: "identity-id",
    repoId: "repo-id",
    permission: "read",
  })
  .then(() => {
    console.log("Read access granted");
  });

// Grant read-write access
sandboxes
  .grantPermission({
    identityId: "identity-id",
    repoId: "repo-id",
    permission: "write",
  })
  .then(() => {
    console.log("Write access granted");
  });

// List permissions for an identity
sandboxes
  .listPermissions({
    identityId: "identity-id",
  })
  .then((permissions) => {
    console.log(permissions);
  });

// Revoke access
sandboxes
  .revokePermission({
    identityId: "identity-id",
    repoId: "repo-id",
  })
  .then(() => {
    console.log("Access revoked");
  });

```

### Create Repository and Request Dev Server

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/dev-servers/dev-servers

Demonstrates how to create a new repository using the Freestyle SDK and then request a development server for that repository. The `repo_id` obtained from creation is used to provision the dev server.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

repo = client.create_repo(
    name="my-new-repo",
    description="A repo created with the Freestyle SDK",
    private=False,
)

print(f"Created repo with ID: {repo.repo_id}")

# Then, you can request a dev server for the repo you just created.
dev_server = client.request_dev_server(repo_id=repo.repo_id)

print(f"Dev Server URL: {dev_server.ephemeral_url}")
```

### Set up OpenAI Python SDK

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/code-execution/integrations/openai

Demonstrates how to initialize the OpenAI client with an API key and execute a chat completion request using a specified model and messages. It also shows how to process the response using a runner function.

```python
import openai
import os

client = openai.OpenAI(
    api_key=os.environ.get("OPENAI_API_KEY"),
)

query = "What is the sum of every number from 50 to 65 divided by 17"
messages = [{"role": "user", "content": query}]

res = client.chat.completions.create(
    model="gpt-4-turbo", messages=messages, tools=[definition]
)

result = runner(res.choices[0].message)
```

```javascript
 apiKey: 'your-api-key',
});

sandboxes.getLogs({
 deploymentId: 'deployment-id',
}).then((response) => {
 console.log(response);
```

### LLM Text Generation with Freestyle.sh (JavaScript)

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/

Illustrates text generation using an LLM in a JavaScript environment integrated with Freestyle.sh. This example highlights the client-side or Node.js usage for interacting with LLM services, including prompt formatting and response handling. Ensure the Freestyle.sh LLM SDK is properly installed and configured.

```javascript
import { LLMClient } from 'freestyle-sh-llm';

// Initialize the LLM client
const llmClient = new LLMClient();

// Define the prompt
const prompt = "Describe the process of photosynthesis in simple terms.";

// Generate text
llmClient.generateText({ prompt: prompt, maxTokens: 100 })
  .then(response => {
    console.log(response.text);
  })
  .catch(error => {
    console.error("Error generating text:", error);
  });
```

--------------------------------

### GitHub Synchronization Architecture

Source: https://context7_llms

Details the technical architecture behind Freestyle's GitHub integration, including the role of GitHub Apps, webhook processing, bidirectional sync, and conflict detection mechanisms.

```markdown
## How It Works

Freestyle's GitHub integration uses GitHub Apps to provide secure, repository-specific access. When you push code to either platform, changes are automatically synchronized to the other, ensuring both repositories stay in sync.

### Architecture

1. **GitHub App**: You own the custom Github app with repository permissions for secure access to the repositories on Github
2. **Webhook Processing**: You get real-time notifications when code changes occur on Github or on Freestyle
3. **Bidirectional Sync**: When a change is made on the Github repository, its proactively synced to the Freestyle repository, and vice versa
4. **Conflict Detection**: We prevents data loss by detecting diverged branches before applying changes
```

--------------------------------

### Tag Object Structure

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Defines the structure of a Tag object. Includes the tag name, optional tagger information, message, and the target object's SHA.

```typescript
interface TagObject {
  // The tag name
  name: string;
  // The tagger (may be null for lightweight tags)
  tagger?: {
    date: string;
    name: string;
    email: string;
  };
  // The tag message (may be null for lightweight tags)
  message?: string;
  // The object this tag points to (usually a commit)
  target: {
    sha: string;
  };
  // The tag's hash
  sha: string;
}
```

### Serve Static Files with Hono

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Sets up a simple Hono server to serve static files generated by Expo. It configures the server to use the './dist' directory for static assets and falls back to 'index.html'.

```typescript
import { Hono } from "hono";
import { serveStatic } from "hono/deno";

const app = new Hono();

app.use("*", serveStatic({ root: "./dist" }));

// fallback to index.html
app.get("*", serveStatic({ path: "./dist/index.html" }));

Deno.serve(app.fetch);
```

--------------------------------

### SSR Server Entrypoint with Hono

Source: https://context7_llms

JavaScript code for the server entrypoint (`index.js`) using Hono. It serves static files and handles SSR rendering by integrating with Vite's server output.

```javascript
import fs from "node:fs/promises";
import { Hono } from "hono";
import { serveStatic } from "hono/deno";
import { render } from "./server/entry-server.js";

const templateHtml = await fs.readFile("./client/index.html", "utf-8");

const app = new Hono();

app.use("*", serveStatic({}));

app.get("*", async (c) => {
  try {
    const url = c.req.url;
    const template = templateHtml;
    const rendered = render(url);

    const html = template
      .replace(`<!--app-head-->`, rendered.head ?? "")
      .replace(`<!--app-html-->`, rendered.html ?? "");

    return c.html(html);
  } catch (e) {
    console.log(e.stack);
    return c.text(e.stack, 500);
  }
});

Deno.serve(app.fetch);
```

```English
Connect an Apple TV to your tailnet for viewing media server files.
```
