### Execute Script with Node Modules

Source: https://context7_llms

Demonstrates how to execute a script using Freestyle's sandboxes, specifying custom node modules and their versions. This allows for the inclusion of external libraries like 'axios' for API calls within the execution environment.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

api
  .executeScript(
    `import axios from 'axios';

    export default async () => {
      // Fetch data from an external API
      const res = await axios.get('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/todos/1');
      return res.data;
    }`,
    {
      nodeModules: {
        axios: "0.21.1", // specify the version of the module you want to use
      },
    }
  )
  .then((result) => {
    console.log("Result: ", result);
  });
```

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

result = client.execute_script(
    code="""

    import axios from 'axios';

    export default async () => {
        // Fetch data from an external API
        const res = await axios.get('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/todos/1');
        return res.data;
    }
    """,
    freestyle.FreestyleExecuteScriptParamsConfiguration(
      node_modules={
        "axios": "0.21.1"  # specify the version of the module you want to use
      }
    )
  ),
)
print(f"Result: {result.result}")
```

### Deploy Next.js App (TypeScript)

Source: https://context7_llms

Deploys a Next.js application from a GitHub repository to Freestyle using the Freestyle Sandboxes SDK. It configures the deployment with a specified domain and enables automatic code building.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

api
  .deployWeb(
    {
      kind: "git",
      url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-base-nextjs-shadcn", // URL of the repository you want to deploy
    },
    {
      domains: ["yourtestdomain.style.dev"],
      build: true, // automatically detects the framework and builds the code
    }
  )
  .then((result) => {
    console.log("Deployed website @ ", result.domains);
  });
```

### Revamping Docs for AI Accessibility

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

This section explains the strategy behind revamping Freestyle's documentation to be more accessible to AI models. It highlights issues with relative URLs and HTML/CSS/JS content, and the solution of using raw markdown.

```javascript
import { cursorUrl, vscodeUrl } from "../../../src/lib/cursor-link";
```

```markdown
## Background

Freestyle is [a cloud to run AI Code](/). We provide a series of tools to manage code written by AI Agents. The tools we're building are weird, as they are oriented at new problems relating to untrusted code that haven't been discussed much before. Without a lot of explanation they can be hard to understand.

We try to regularly have coffee, and hack days with our customers. Over the course of hack days a few weeks ago, we noticed the way we were being used had changed. Our users didn't want to read our docs, they wanted to ask AI questions about them — and AI was giving them the wrong answers. We went through a pivot 11 months ago, and half the time it was still responding about our old product. Sometimes it hallucinated APIs we didn't have, and we even once heard of it giving code snippets referencing how to use one of our competitors!

## How we revamped our Docs for AI

We decided to add a series of functionalities to our docs to make them more accessible to AI, and therefore our users. They are as follows:

### LLMs.txt

We started with an [llms.txt](/llms.txt) and [llms-full.txt](/llms-full.txt) that we generated from our content. However, we did it badly.

Our first generation of the llms.txt files used **relative urls**. This meant that users who copy and pasted the file into their own agents couldn't get anything. Further, a lot of AI docs scrapers are bad, and just didn't handle relative urls at all.

Once we fixed that, we still originally linked directly to docs pages. This made AI clients reading the pages read the full html/css/js of the page and not just the text. The worst side effect of this is that we have lots of tab views in our docs that default to JavaScript, when AI Scrapers would read these pages they wouldn't get any Python documentation for our Python users. So we re-exported all of our docs files with a `.md` extension — any page on this website can be gone to with .md at the end of the URL and it will return the raw markdown content of the page, here's [this page](/blog/docs-revamp.md) as markdown.
```

--------------------------------

### Git on VM as Source of Truth - Drawbacks

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

This section details the limitations of using Git on a VM as the source of truth. While it introduces version control, it still faces challenges with scalability, portability, backup, and performance bottlenecks due to VM access requirements for Git operations.

```markdown
- Scalability issues
- Portability issues
- Backup issues
- Performance bottlenecks
- Increased runtime cost
```

### Create Domain Verification Request

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Creates a domain verification request with Freestyle using Python. This process involves generating a verification code that needs to be added as a TXT DNS record for the domain.

```python
import freestyle

client = freestyle.Freestyle("YOUR_FREESTYLE_API_KEY")

verification_request = client.create_domain_verification_request(
    domain="yourdomain.com" # this also works for subdomains
)

print("Domain verification request created successfully!")
print(f"Domain: {verification_request.domain}")
print(f"Verification Code: {verification_request.verification_code}")
print(f"Id: {verification_request.id}")

```

### Git on VM as Source of Truth - Drawbacks

Source: https://context7_llms

This section discusses the limitations of using Git on a VM as the source of truth. While it introduces version control, it still faces challenges with scalability, portability, backup, and performance bottlenecks due to VM access requirements for Git operations.

```text
While you can track changes and collaborate better, you still face issues with scalability, portability, and backup. The VM must still be accessed for every Git operation, which can lead to performance bottlenecks and increased runtime cost.
```

### Footer Configuration

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Defines the structure and content of the website's footer, including copyright information, call-to-action buttons, logo grids, and navigation links. This configuration is likely used in a web framework to dynamically render the footer.

```json
{
  "errorScripts": null,
  "template": [
    "$",
    "$Lb",
    null,
    {}
  ],
  "templateStyles": null,
  "templateScripts": null,
  "notFound": null,
  "notFoundStyles": null
}
```

```json
{
```

### Manage Git Access Tokens

Source: https://context7_llms

Provides functionality to create, list, and revoke access tokens for a given Git identity. Access tokens are used for authentication.

```javascript
// Create a token for an identity
sandboxes
  .createGitToken({
    identityId: "identity-id",
  })
  .then((token) => {
    console.log(token.value); // Store this securely
  });

// List tokens for an identity
sandboxes
  .listGitTokens({
    identityId: "identity-id",
  })
  .then((tokens) => {
    console.log(tokens);
  });

// Revoke a token
sandboxes
  .revokeGitToken({
    identityId: "identity-id",
    tokenId: "token-id",
  })
  .then(() => {
    console.log("Token revoked");
  });
```

### Cursor Integration for Freestyle Documentation

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/getting-started

Adds Freestyle documentation to your Cursor IDE setup, enabling easy referencing of API documentation while coding. This uses a custom URI scheme to install the documentation.

```javascript
cursor://anysphere.cursor-deeplink/mcp/install?name=freestyle-documentation&config=ewogICJuYW1lIjogImZyZWVzdHlsZS1kb2N1bWVudGF0aW9uIiwKICAiY29tbWFuZCI6ICJucHgiLAogICJhcmdzIjogWwogICAgIi15IiwKICAgICJtY3AtcmVtb3RlIiwKICAgICJodHRwczovL2RvY3MuZnJlZXN0eWxlLnNoL2FwaS9tY3AvbWNwIgogIF0KfQ%3D%3D
```

### Execute Script with Custom Node Modules

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Demonstrates how to execute a script in a Freestyle sandbox, specifying custom Node.js modules and their versions. This allows for the use of external libraries like 'axios' to interact with external APIs.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const api = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!, // make sure to set this
});

api
  .executeScript(
    `import axios from 'axios';

    export default async () => {
      // Fetch data from an external API
      const res = await axios.get('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/todos/1');
      return res.data;
    }`,
    {
      nodeModules: {
        axios: "0.21.1", // specify the version of the module you want to use
      },
    }
  )
  .then((result) => {
    console.log("Result: ", result);
  });
```

### Create Database Record Example

Source: https://modelcontextprotocol.io/legacy/concepts/tools

This snippet demonstrates the creation of a database record with various hints like readOnlyHint, destructiveHint, idempotentHint, and openWorldHint. It's a configuration example for how such records might be defined or managed.

```typescript
server.setRequestHandler(ListToolsRequestSchema, 
  async (request, response) => {
    const result = await listTools(request.body);
    response.send(result);
  }
);

// Example of creating a database record with hints
const createDatabaseRecord = (hints: {
  readOnlyHint?: boolean;
  destructiveHint?: boolean;
  idempotentHint?: boolean;
  openWorldHint?: boolean;
}) => {
  // ... implementation to create record ...
  return {
    success: true,
    message: "Record created successfully"
  };
};

// Usage example:
const recordConfig = {
  readOnlyHint: false,
  destructiveHint: false,
  idempotentHint: false,
  openWorldHint: false
};

createDatabaseRecord(recordConfig);
```

--------------------------------

### Tag Object Structure

Source: https://context7_llms

Defines the structure of a Tag object. Includes the tag name, optional tagger information, message, and the target object's SHA.

```typescript
interface TagObject {
  // The tag name
  name: string;
  // The tagger (may be null for lightweight tags)
  tagger?: {
    date: string;
    name: string;
    email: string;
  };
  // The tag message (may be null for lightweight tags)
  message?: string;
  // The object this tag points to (usually a commit)
  target: {
    sha: string;
  };
  // The tag's hash
  sha: string;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Freestyle Git API Overview

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Details the capabilities of the Freestyle Git API for managing Git repositories, access control, and automation triggers, specifically for AI app builders. It emphasizes multi-tenancy, identity management, and integration features.

```APIDOC
Freestyle Git API:
  - Manages Git repositories, access permissions, and automation triggers.
  - Natively Multi-Tenant: Designed for managing repositories for multiple users and organizations.
  - Robust Identity Management: Built-in identity management for creating and managing identities with fine-grained access control.
  - Seamless Integration: Triggers system for easy collaboration with CI/CD systems and external services.
  - GitHub Sync: Built-in synchronization with GitHub, including app/auth management.
```

--------------------------------

### Git API for Code Management

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Describes the Git API provided by Freestyle for managing AI-generated code. It emphasizes the benefits of using Git for version control, collaboration, debugability, portability, and integration with CI/CD pipelines for live previews and deployments.

```APIDOC
Git API:
  Purpose: Manages repositories for AI-generated code.
  Benefits:
    - Version Control: History, reverting, branching, merging.
    - Collaboration: Multiple agents working together.
    - Debugability: Track AI's process, clone prototypes.
    - Portability: Sync to GitHub, allow local cloning.
    - Integration: Live previews, automatic deployments via CI/CD.
```

```python
content = fs.read_file("src/index.tsx")

    print(content)
```

--------------------------------

### Create Git Repository (JavaScript)

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/dev-servers/dev-servers

Demonstrates how to create a Git repository using the Freestyle Sandboxes SDK in JavaScript. This includes setting repository properties like name, public access, and source URL.

```javascript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes();


const { repoId } = await freestyle.createGitRepository({
  name: "Test Repository",

  // This will make it easy for us to clone the repo during testing.
  // The repo won't be listed on any public registry, but anybody
  // with the uuid can clone it. You should disable this in production.
  public: true,

  source: {
    url: "https://github.com/freestyle-sh/freestyle-next",
    type: "git",
  },
});

console.log(`Created repo with ID: ${repoId}`);
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale Messages

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Information regarding messages, alerts, or notifications displayed by Tailscale clients or the admin console.

```APIDOC
Tailscale Messages:

Types of Messages:
  - **Informational**: Notifications about successful operations or status updates.
  - **Warnings**: Indicate potential issues or configurations that might lead to problems.
  - **Errors**: Signify failures in operations, requiring user intervention.
  - **Security Alerts**: Notify about potential security risks or policy violations.

Examples:
  - "Tailscale is running. Connected to your tailnet."
  - "Warning: Device is advertising routes but is not tagged as a subnet router."
  - "Error: Failed to connect to the control server. Check your network connection."
  - "Security Alert: An unknown device attempted to join your tailnet."

Viewing Messages:
  - Tailscale client logs often contain detailed message information.
  - The Tailscale admin console may display important alerts or notifications.

```

```bash
npm install freestyle-sandboxes ai @ai-sdk/react @ai-sdk/anthropic @modelcontextprotocol/sdk
```

### Next.js Server Action for Dev Server

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/dev-servers/dev-servers

Example of a Next.js server action that starts or returns the status of a Freestyle dev server. It imports the freestyle library and defines an asynchronous function `requestDevServer`.

```ts
"use server";
import { freestyle } from "@/lib/freestyle";

export async function requestDevServer({
  repo,
  branch,
}: { repo: string; branch: string }) {
  return freestyle.requestDevServer(repo, branch);
}
```

--------------------------------

### GitHub Sync Configuration API Reference

Source: https://context7_llms

Provides details on configuring GitHub synchronization programmatically via the API. This includes the endpoint and parameters required for setting up the sync between Freestyle and GitHub repositories. Note that the Python SDK does not yet support this functionality.

```APIDOC
Endpoint: /API-Reference/git/configure_github_sync

Method: POST (or relevant HTTP method)

Description: Configures bidirectional synchronization between a Freestyle repository and a GitHub repository.

Parameters:
  repoId (string): The unique identifier for the Freestyle repository.
  githubRepoName (string): The full name of the GitHub repository in the format 'owner/repository-name'.

Prerequisites:
  - The GitHub App must be installed on the specified GitHub repository.
  - The user or service account making the API call must have the necessary permissions.

Example Usage (Conceptual):
POST /API-Reference/git/configure_github_sync
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "repoId": "your-freestyle-repo-id",
  "githubRepoName": "user/repo-name"
}

Response:
  - Success: 200 OK or 201 Created with confirmation.
  - Error: 400 Bad Request (e.g., invalid repoId, repo not found), 403 Forbidden (e.g., insufficient permissions), 404 Not Found (e.g., GitHub repository not found).

Related Information:
  - Freestyle SDKs (JavaScript supports this, Python does not yet).
  - Admin Dashboard for manual configuration and status monitoring.
```

### Creating a Domain Mapping

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Illustrates how to create a new domain mapping using the Freestyle API. This maps a specified domain to a particular deployment ID. If the domain is already mapped, this operation updates the existing mapping.

```typescript
import {
  Freestyle
} from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new Freestyle({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!,
});

async function createDomainMapping() {
  const result = await freestyle.insertDomainMapping({
    domain: "example.style.dev",
    deploymentId: "deployment-id", // The ID of the deployment you want to map the domain to
  });

  console.log("Created domain mapping:", result);
}
```

### Configure Expo for Server Mode

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Configures the Expo project to use 'server' output mode in app.json. This enables support for Expo API Routes and server-side rendering.

```json
{
  "expo": {
    "web": {
      "bundler": "metro",
      "output": "server" // [!code ++]
    }
  }
}
```

### Homepage UI for Creating New Apps

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

This React component provides a simple homepage with a button to create a new app. Clicking the button calls the `createChat` function, initiates the app creation process, and redirects the user to the newly created app's page. It manages a loading state to provide user feedback.

```tsx
import { useState } from "react";
import { useRouter } from "next/navigation";

import { createChat } from "../lib/create-chat";

export default function Home() {
  const router = useRouter();
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);

  async function handleClick() {
    setLoading(true);
    const { repoId } = await createChat();
    router.push(`/app/${repoId}`);
  }

  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col items-center justify-center h-screen">
      <h1 className="text-4xl font-bold">AI App Builder</h1>
      <button
        className="px-4 py-2 mt-4 text-white bg-blue-500 rounded"
        onClick={handleClick}
        disabled={loading}
      >
        {loading ? "Creating..." : "Create App"}
      </button>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Human-in-the-Loop for AI Agents

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Recommends more aggressive human-in-the-loop systems for managing MCPs and AI agent actions. It highlights companies like Humanlayer and their work on orchestration and state/context management as critical challenges in human-in-the-loop systems.

```APIDOC
Human-in-the-Loop (HITL) for MCPs:
  Requirement: Implement aggressive HITL systems for MCP oversight.
  Key Challenges (as per Humanlayer's 12-factor-agents):
    - Orchestration
    - State/Context Management
  Providers: Companies like Humanlayer offer tools for AI agent monitoring.
```

```APIDOC
Security Best Practices:
  - Key and secret management: Securely manage authentication keys and secrets.
  - Secret scanning: Implement measures to detect and prevent secret leakage.
  - Admin with passkey: Use passkeys for enhanced administrative security.
```

### Create a Git Repository from an Existing Repository

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Creates a new Git repository by cloning an existing Git repository. You can specify the branch and whether to perform a shallow clone. Note: Currently, there is no support for private repositories from outside of Freestyle.

```javascript
sandboxes.createGitRepository({
  name: 'cloned-example',
  source: {
    type: 'git',
    url: 'https://github.com/freestyle-sh/cloudstate',
    branch: 'main' // Optional: specify branch to checkout
    depth: 0, // Optional: shallow clone
  }
}).then(res => {
  console.log(res.repoId);
});

```

--------------------------------

### Blob Object Structure

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Defines the structure of a Blob object returned by the API. Includes the base64 encoded content, encoding type, and the blob's SHA hash.

```typescript
interface BlobObject {
  // The blob content (base64 encoded)
  content: string;
  // Always "base64"
  encoding: "base64";
  // The blob's hash
  sha: string;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Tailscale SSH Session Recording

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

Details how to configure and utilize Tailscale SSH session recording to capture and review SSH activity on your nodes.

```APIDOC
SSH Session Recording:

Configuration:
  Enable SSH on your nodes via the Tailscale admin console or CLI.
  Set the `ssh` option in your policy file to `record` or `debug`.

Example Policy:
  "group:devs" -> "tag:dev-servers": [
    { "port": 22, "action": "accept", "ssh": "record" },
  ];

Accessing Recordings:
  SSH session recordings are typically stored on the node itself.
  The exact location may vary based on the operating system and Tailscale version.
  Refer to the Tailscale documentation for specific paths.

```

### Tailscale User Invitation and Device Management

Source: https://tailscale.com/kb/1017/install

This section details how to invite external users to your Tailscale tailnet and manage device additions. It covers inviting users via email or invite links, and methods for adding servers and managing devices through MDM.

```APIDOC
APIDOC:
  Invite External Users:
    Description: Allows inviting users not part of your custom domain (e.g., contractors, friends, family).
    Methods:
      - Invite via email: Send one or more invites directly to user email addresses.
      - Copy invite link: Share a link that directs users to the Tailscale login page for authentication.
    Process:
      1. Navigate to the 'Users' page in the admin console.
      2. Select 'Invite external users'.
      3. Choose either 'Invite via email' or 'Copy invite link'.
      4. Invited users authenticate via a supported SSO identity provider and are added to the 'Users' page.
    Related:
      - KB Article: /kb/1271/invite-any-user

  Add Devices to Tailnet:
    Description: Methods for adding devices to your Tailscale network.
    Methods:
      - Log in: Access the tailnet from other devices using an existing user account.
      - Add servers: Provision servers using an authentication key and a tag for identity. Refer to 'Setting up a server on your Tailscale network' for details.
      - Integrate with MDM: Incorporate system policies like Mobile Device Management (MDM) for device control. Refer to 'Integrate with an MDM solution' for details.
    Features:
      - Automatic IP Assignment: Each device receives a unique 100.x.y.z IP address for stable connections, even behind firewalls or when networks change.
    Related:
      - KB Article: /kb/1316/device-add
      - KB Article: /kb/1068/tags
      - KB Article: /kb/1085/auth-keys
      - KB Article: /kb/1245/set-up-servers
      - KB Article: /kb/1362/mdm
      - KB Article: /kb/1033/ip-and-dns-addresses
      - KB Article: /blog/how-nat-traversal-works
```

### NextJS FreestyleDevServer Component

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

A React component for NextJS that automatically keeps the dev server alive. It uses a provided server action to request and manage the dev server.

```tsx
import { FreestyleDevServer } from "freestyle-sandboxes/react/dev-server";
import { requestDevServer } from "./preview-actions";

export function Preview({ repoId }: { repoId: string }) {
  <FreestyleDevServer actions={{ requestDevServer }} repoId={repoId} />;
}
```

### Request Dev Server

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/llms-full.txt

Requests a dev server instance for a given repository ID. The dev server will automatically run 'npm run dev' and will shut down if not kept alive. It provides an ephemeral URL for accessing the running application.

```typescript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes();

const devServer = await freestyle.requestDevServer({ repoId });

console.log(`Dev Server URL: ${devServer.ephemeralUrl}`);

```

--------------------------------

### MCP for Tool Sharing

Source: https://context7_llms

Explains how MCP (Model Context Protocol) revolutionized tool sharing among AI metaframeworks and models. Before MCP, sharing code executors required individual packages for each integration, which was cumbersome. MCP provides a standard for easy tool sharing.

```English
Before MCP existed, Freestyle wanted to share our code executor with other companies, so in order to share it we were forced to create individual packages for [every AI Metaframework and model we wanted to support](/code-execution/integrations/vercel) — this sucked, which is why most companies didn't bother, a few did.

In November 2024, [MCP](https://www.anthropic.com/news/model-context-protocol) changed this, creating a standard that makes it easy for any team to share tools with agents, and for any agent to use them.
```

--------------------------------

### Deploy Web Action

Source: https://context7_llms

Defines a server action to deploy a web application by referencing its Git repository. This action automatically fetches the latest code, builds it, and deploys it to specified domains. It also allows for setting environment variables for the deployment.

```ts
"use server";
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY,
});

export async function deployAction(
  repoId: string, // [!code highlight] the repoId for your app
  domains: string[] // [!code highlight] the domains you want to deploy to
) {
  const { domains } = await freestyle.deployWeb(
    {
      kind: "git",
      repoUrl: `https://git.freestyle.sh/${repoId}`,
    },
    {
      domains,
      envVars: {
        // ... any environment variables you want to set
      },
    }
  );
}
```

--------------------------------

### Initialize Freestyle Sandboxes

Source: https://docs.freestyle.sh/guides/app-builder

Imports the FreestyleSandboxes class and creates an instance, configuring it with an API key from environment variables. This is the primary setup for using the Freestyle Sandboxes service.

```javascript
import { FreestyleSandboxes } from "freestyle-sandboxes";

const freestyle = new FreestyleSandboxes({
  apiKey: process.env.FREESTYLE_API_KEY!
});
```
